This article refers to the
son of Dáin II Ironfoot
. For other namesakes, see
Thorin (disambiguation)
.
Thorin III
Biographical information
Titles
Stonehelm,
King of Durin's Folk
,
King under the Mountain
Birth
TA 2866
Rule
TA 3019
Death
Early
Fourth Age
Realms
Iron Hills
Lonely Mountain
Physical description
Race
Dwarves
Height
About 4'0" at least
Culture
Durin's Folk
Thorin III "Stonehelm"
was the son and heir of
Dáin II
of
Durin's Folk
, who was king of the
Dwarves
of
Erebor
and the
Iron Hills
in
Rhovanion
.
Biography
Thorin III was born in the Iron Hills to Lord Dáin Ironfoot. During his younger years he saw his people able to finally return to the Lonely Mountain after many years of further exile, and wandering. He himself became a prince with the accession of his father as
King under the Mountain
, and over all the
Longbeards
.
During the
Great War of the Ring
at the age of one hundred fifty-three, Thorin fought the
Easterlings
in the
Battle of Dale
, and took refuge in the Lonely Mountain after his father was killed at its gates, along with
Brand
, the
King of Dale
. Thorin then became King under the Mountain.
When the news of
Sauron
's defeat in the South came to the ears of the enemy, they became dismayed and the Dwarves and Men came forth from the mountain and routed them, driving them back to the river
Redwater
, never troubling them again.
With his father's death, Thorin became king in
TA 3019
. Thorin III helped rebuild the Lonely Mountain and
Dale
, and prospered. His realm became a close ally of the
Reunited Kingdom
of
Arnor
and
Gondor
of
King
Elessar
.
During his rule,
Gimli
, son of
Glóin
, led a number of Dwarves south to the
Glittering Caves
, where a new city was settled.
Thorin III had a descendant, who was held to be the reincarnation of Durin the Deathless and who, at the death of his unnamed father, succeeded him as
Durin VII
the Last.
Thorin III Stonehelm (2001
Trading Card
image)
In adaptations
Middle-earth Strategy Battle Game
Thorin's miniature in the
Middle-earth Strategy Battle Game
Thorin III Stonehelm is featured in the
Middle-earth Strategy Battle Game
, introduced in the 2022 supplement
Defence of the North
which focused on the events surrounding the
Battle of Dale
. Thorin is said to possess a calmer and more cool-headed nature than Dain, which gives him better tactical insight upon the battlefield. During the Battle of Dale Thorin comes into his own, driving back the Easterling forces from Erebor and avenging Dain's death.
Lord of the Rings Online
Thorin III in
The Lord of the Rings Online
In
The Lord of the Rings Online
, Thorin III is a major character. Although the player does not meet him until after the downfall of
Sauron
, as the new King of the Longbeards he becomes prominent in multiple storylines concerning
Mordor
,
Eryn Lasgalen
,
Dale
-lands, the
Iron Hills
,
Ered Mithrin
and even
Moria
.

PAGE: Three Elderwomen of the Elves

"And while I can honestly say I have told you the truth, I may not have told you all of it."
At least part of this article or section is of insufficient length or lacks important details. Please
expand it
if you can.
The
Three Elderwomen of the Elves
were the spouses to the three
Elf-fathers
who were among the
first
144
Elves
to
awaken
by the bay of
Cuiviénen
on the inland
Sea of Helcar
. Their names were
Iminyë
,
Tatië
, and
Enelyë
. Their husbands are (respectively)
Imin
,
Tata
, and
Enel
.
After
Oromë
first
found
the Elves, he taught the Three Elderwomen of the Elves the art of making
lembas
from the
Western Corn
seeds he brought from
Aman
. The Three Elderwomen of the Elves later became the first
Massánië
and founded the
Hávanissi
.

PAGE: Tobold Hornblower
CATEGORIES: Hobbits
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Tobold_Hornblower
======================================================================

This article refers to the
Hobbit who discovered Pipe-weed
. For other namesakes, see
Horn (disambiguation)
.
Tobold Hornblower
, also called
Old Toby
, was a
hobbit
of the
Shire
.
Biography
Tobold was a well-respected gardener, most notable for his discovery and cultivation of the herb
Pipe-weed
c.
TA 2670
, or 1070 by
Shire Reckoning
. He resided in the
Southfarthing
village of
Longbottom
, and was there immortalized as 'Old Toby'. His Pipe-weed business led to the herb's popularity throughout the Shire and beyond.
The Pipe-weed variety 'Old Toby' was named after him, and 'Longbottom Leaf' possibly refers to his home where the plant was first cultivated in the Shire. According to
Herblore of the Shire
, by
Meriadoc Brandybuck
, it was believed that Tobold Hornblower learned about Pipe-weed in
Bree
, as that was the farthest from the Shire that he traveled and the herb was known to have grown on the south slopes of the hill there. His date of death is not recorded, but he likely died sometime in the twenty-seventh century of the
Third Age
.
See also
Old Toby (disambiguation)

Tolman Cotton Jr.
Biographical information
Birth
TA 2980
(SR 1380)
Death
FO 60
(SR 1481)

Physical description
Race
Hobbits
Gender
Male
Tolman Cotton Jr.
or
Tom Cotton Jr.
was a
Hobbit
of the
Shire
.
Biography
Tom was born in
TA 2980
(SR 1380), four years before Rosie. He was the eldest son of
Farmer Cotton
. He had four younger siblings;
Rosie Cotton
,
Wilcome (Jolly) Cotton
,
Bowman (Nick) Cotton
, and
Carl (Nibs) Cotton
.
He played a significant role in the
Battle of Bywater
and fought alongside his father. Afterwards, he married
Marigold
, who was three years his junior. She was as well, the younger sister of
Samwise Gamgee
, who also just so happened to marry Tom's younger sister Rosie. He served briefly as Deputy-Mayor of
Michel Delving
when Sam went to
Gondor
.
Because the Cottons were so close to the Gamgees, and Sam was the same age as Tom, you could expect that they were good friends growing up, and later on in life.
Portrayal in adaptations
Tolman Cotton Jr. made an appearance in
The Lord of the Rings: Aragorn's Quest
and was the Deputy-Mayor (
The Lord of the Rings: Aragorn's Quest
)

Tolman Gamgee
was a
Hobbit
of the
Shire
. Born in
FO 21
(
SR 1442
), he was the seventh son and thirteenth and final child of
Samwise Gamgee
and his wife,
Rosie (née Cotton) Gamgee
. His eldest sibling,
Elanor
, was twenty-one years his senior.
There were two other family members with whom Tolman shared his name. First was his uncle
Tolman Cotton Jr.
, and then his maternal grandfather
Tolman Cotton
. Both them fought in the
Battle of Bywater
.
His grandfather
Tolman
was known as Farmer Cotton, and was a great leader for the lower class of the
Shire
.
[
citation needed
]
Frodo
did not foresee Tolman to Sam.

Túrin I
was the sixth
Ruling Steward of Gondor
.
Biography
Born in TA 2165, Túrin I was the third child and only son of
Húrin I
and was likely named after the
First Age
hero,
Túrin Turambar
.
Following the death of his father, Húrin I, in
TA 2244
Túrin I became the sixth Ruling Steward of
Gondor
, and the sixth steward to rule during the era known as the
Watchful Peace
. Twice married, Túrin had several daughters and one son.
Túrin's youngest child and his only son
Hador
was born in
TA 2245
when Turin was eighty years old.
Túrin I died in the year TA 2278 after thirty-four years of rule at the age of 113 years old and was succeeded by his son Hador.
Etymology
The name
Túrin
comes from the
Sindarin
tur
("power, mastery").
It should be pronounced as
too-rin.

======================================================================
PAGE: Valacar
CATEGORIES: Kings of Gondor, Men of Gondor
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Valacar
======================================================================

Valacar
Biographical information
Titles
King of Gondor
Birth
TA 1194
Rule
TA 1366
-
TA 1432
(66 Years)
Death
TA 1432
(aged 238)
Realms
Gondor
Spouse
Vidumavi
Weapon
King's
sword
Physical description
Race
Men
Gender
Male
Culture
Dúnedain
(
Gondorians
)
Valacar
was the twentieth
King of Gondor
and the son of
Rómendacil II
, whom he succeeded in
TA 1366
.
Biography
Valacar was born in the year
1194
during the
Third Age
.
Valacar's father,
Minalcar
, the regent of Gondor, sent Valacar as an ambassador to
Vidugavia
, a prince of the
Northmen
who called himself "
King
of
Rhovanion
". Minalcar charged Valacar to learn the language, manners and policies of the Northmen. During his stay in
Rhovanion
, Valacar learned to love the country and the Northmen. With the approval of his father,
Valacar married
Vidumavi
, the daughter of Vidugavia in that time.
In the year
1250
,
his son
Vinitharya
was born. Valacar was recalled back to Gondor in the year
1260
by his father to take part in the councils of the realm and the command of its armies.
Along with Vidumavi and Vinitharya, Valacar was accompanied by a household of noble men and women from Rhovanion.
They were mostly welcomed in Gondor and Valacar gave his son the name Eldacar for public use in Gondor.
However, the high men of Gondor disapproved of Valacar's marriage to Vidumavi, who had a shorter lifespan than the Dúnedain because the Northmen were
Middle Men
. Some conservative Gondorians feared that Eldacar's descendants would also have a short life and weaken the
Númenórean
blood of the kings. Thus, they did not want to accept Eldacar as their lord. When Valacar grew old, rebellion smoldered in the
southern provinces
.
Valacar ruled Gondor for sixty-six years, and was succeeded by Eldacar when he died in the year
1432
.
After Valacar's death, the rebellion turned into a civil war known as the
Kin-strife
.
This conflict lasted for fifteen years, until Eldacar secured the throne.
Etymology
Valacar
is a name in
Quenya
that possibly meant "Vala helm"
since it is a compound of the word
vala
("a Power; angelic power") and
-car

PAGE: Valandil (The Lost Road)
CATEGORIES: Númenóreans
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Valandil_(The_Lost_Road)
======================================================================

!
The canonicity of this subject is uncertain.
The precise canonical status of this article's subject is unclear.
To find out about what is considered "canon" see
LOTR:Canon
.
!
This article is about the
character in
The Lost Road
story
. For the other namesakes, see
Valandil (disambiguation)
.
Valandil
Physical description
Race
Men
Gender
Male
Culture
Númenóreans
(
Faithful
)
Valandil
was a
Númenórean
noblemen and the father of
Elendil
according to the early version of the
legendarium
in
The Lost Road
.
Biography
When
Herendil
informed his father that though the two of them are the blood of kings, his peers called him names such as "Terendul" the day prior, and accused him of being a "half-Noldo",
Elendil
responded by saying that then it may be dangerous for Herendil to be his son as his own father's name, Valandil, meant "God-friend".
Later. Elendil tells his son that he cannot be corrupted by the servants of
Morgoth
due to Valandil his father being the "chief of the wise men of
Númenor
".
Etymology
Valandil
is a name in
Quenya
meaning "God-friend", being a compound of
vanan
("god") +
(-n)dil
("friend").
Oswine
was it's
Old English
cognate.
In other versions
In an alternative version, but separate from
The Lost Road
, Valandil was the son of
Amandil
and the brother of
Elendil
the Tall, having the role of
Anarion
and founding
Ondor
.
References

Biographical information

Men

Male
Culture
Númenóreans
Voronwë
was a
Númenórean
noblemen.
Biography
Voronwë was a Man of Númenor and a member of
The Faithful
's faction. He managed to escape with the ships under the command of
Elendil
during the
Akallabêth
, reaching
Middle-earth
along with the future first
king of Arnor
.

means "steadfast" in
Quenya
.
His equivalent in
Adûnaic
was
Abrazân
.

PAGE: Wellinghall
CATEGORIES: Ents
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Wellinghall
======================================================================

Merry and Pippin stay in Wellinghall
Wellinghall
was the name of one of the
Ent
Treebeard
's houses in
Fangorn Forest
.
It lay near the
Methedras
peak and was surrounded by a host of evergreen trees, which served as a roof and ideal cover. It had one large room with some furniture in it. While in Fangorn Forest on
February 29
,
3019
, the
hobbits
Merry
and
Pippin
drank of Treebeard's magical
Ent-draughts
in Wellinghall, which increased their growth, making them the tallest hobbits on record. Then they spent the night there, the day before the awaited
Entmoot
.
In adaptations
Wellinghall in
The Lord of the Rings Online
In
The Lord of the Rings Online
, Wellinghall was first visited in a flashback narrated by Merry and Pippin, Wellinghall sits empty during the present day after Treebeard had gone to
Isengard
.

======================================================================
PAGE: White Wizard
CATEGORIES: Wizards
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/White_Wizard
======================================================================

"GANDALF WHITE", by
Snezhana Mirkwood
"
Yet it is said that in the ending of the task for which [Gandalf] came he suffered greatly, and was slain, and being sent back from death for a brief while was clothed then in white, and became a radiant flame (yet veiled still save in great need).
"
—
Unfinished Tales of Númenor and Middle-earth
, "
The Istari
"
"
White Wizard
" was the title held by the two chiefs of the
Istari
(Wizards), both sent to help
Free Peoples
of
Middle-earth
in the struggle against the
Dark Lord
Sauron
.
History
Gimli:
"But you are all in white!"
Gandalf:
"‘Yes, I am white now. [...] Indeed I am Saruman, one might almost say, Saruman as he should have been."
—
The Two Towers
, "
The White Rider
"
The first White Wizard was the
Maia
Saruman
(
Curumo
), known to the
Elves
as
Curunír
. Saruman was the first of the Istari to volunteer and, because he was "higher in
Valinórean
stature", he became their chief. In Middle-earth, he was also chosen to lead the
White Council
. But, wanting to "order all the
world
to his will",
he was brought low by his greed and became "an ally, or servant, of Sauron",
albeit coveting the
One Ring
for himself.
"Saruman—Corruption", by
Donato Giancola
The second White Wizard was the wise Maia
Gandalf
(
Olórin
), or
Mithrandir
as the Elves called him. Fearing Sauron and temptation, Gandalf hesitated to go to Middle-earth, but was commanded to do so by
Manwë
, viceregent of
Ilúvatar
. He also joined the White Council, conferring with the lords of the
Eldar
on how to oppose Sauron. Gandalf soon became "the Enemy of Sauron", even sacrificing his life for his mission.
He was then sent back to assume Saruman's mantle and right his wrongs.
Both White Wizards played important parts in shaping the history of the
Third Age
, especially the events that affected
Men
and
Elves
. As "the director and coordinator of both attack and defence" against the Dark Lord,
Gandalf rallied the Free Peoples in their hour of need, ensuring the downfall of Sauron and the
Dominion of Men
. His task done, he left Middle-earth and returned to
Valinor
.
Saruman, on the other hand, failed completely, betraying both the Free Peoples and his "new master".
Even when given the chance "to renounce both
Mordor
and his private schemes",
Saruman refused. In the end, he was defeated in the
Battle of Bywater
and his spirit was barred from returning to Middle-earth.
Trivia
Before his corruption, Saruman was also known as the
White Messenger
.
After being sent back, Gandalf's alias of the "Grey Pilgrim" was altered to the
White Rider
.
Even though he once styled himself as "Saruman of Many Colors",
Saruman's emblem as Lord of
Isengard
was the
White Hand
.
At
Cuiviénen
,
Melian
had acted as chief of the Five Guardians (the future Istari), though she did not hold the mantle of White Wizard.
References

Wilcombe Cotton
,
more commonly known as "
Will
",
was a
Hobbit
of the
Shire
and a member of the
Cotton
family.
Biography
Wilcombe was born in
TA 2946
(
SR 1346
) to
Holman Cotton
and his unnamed wife. He was the brother of
Tolman Cotton
and an uncle to
Rosie Cotton
, the eventual wife of
Samwise Gamgee
. Little else is known of his life, save that he was likely a resident of
Bywater
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Witnesses of Manwë
CATEGORIES: Eagles
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Witnesses_of_Manwë
======================================================================

The
Witnesses of Manwë
were sacred
Great Eagles
of
Manwë
that kept watch upon the great mountain of
Meneltarma
, near to the center of
Mittalmar
in
Númenor
.
History
Meneltarma, the Pillar of the Heavens, was a sacred place of
Eru Ilúvatar
. When anyone approached the summit, three eagles would alight upon three rocks near to its western edge, keeping watch upon the sacred place. They were believed to have been sent from
Aman
to be guardians against those who would do the holy place harm. During the times of the
Three Prayers
the eagles would not descend, but would remain in the sky and hover above all those present at the ceremony.
Translations

Írildë
Biographical information
Birth
SA 700
Death
Unknown
Spouse
Unknown
Physical description
Race
Men
Gender
Female
Culture
Númenóreans
(
House of Elros
)
Írildë
was a
noblewoman
of
Númenór
.
Biography
Írildë was the first child and only daughter of the nobleman
Cemendur
. She had only one sibling, a brother named
Hallatan
. Little of her life is known.
Etymology
"Írildë" is a compound
Quenya
name, likely from the elements
írë
, meaning "desire", and the feminine agental suffix -
ldë
.

PAGE: Îbal
CATEGORIES: Númenóreans
URL: https://lotr.fandom.com/wiki/Îbal
======================================================================

Îbal
Biographical information
Birth
Early
First Age
?
Death
Unknown
Physical description
Race
Men
Gender
Male
Culture
Númenóreans
Îbal
was a
Númenórean
of
Emerië
.
Biography
Îbal was the son of
Ulbar
, a
Man
who once served with the great Númenórean captain and future
King of Númenor
Aldarion
. He was a boy living in the pleasant region of Emerië in the early
Second Age
.
As a boy, he knew
Ancalimë
when she was just a girl and living in the
White House
. He greatly wished to be a mariner like his father had become and to sail the great
seas
of the world. Whether he fulfilled that dream is unknown.
Îbal lived on a farm close to the White House, and would frequently run errands between the two places.
References
